# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully completed the comprehensive analysis of rate limiting middleware patterns in both Envoy and Kubernetes. Here's what I found:

## Summary of Findings

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a detailed analysis covering 24 source files and 15 key symbols across both repositories.

### **Envoy Rate Limiting** (C++ Implementation)
1. **Local Rate Limit Filters** (HTTP, Network, Listener levels)
   - `source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/` - HTTP request rate limiting
   - Uses token bucket with configurable fill intervals and tokens per fill
   - Supports per-connection and global modes

2. **Common Token Bucket Implementation**
   - `source/extensions/filters/common/local_ratelimit/local_ratelimit_impl.h`
   - LocalRateLimiterImpl and RateLimitTokenBucket classes
   - Shared across all filter levels via reusable design

3. **Global Rate Limit Service Client** (Distributed Rate Limiting)
   - `source/extensions/filters/http/rate_limit_quota/global_client_impl.h/cc`
   - Bidirectional gRPC streaming with Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS)
   - LocalRateLimitClientImpl for per-worker thread access via TLS
   - Manages quota buckets across multiple worker threads

### **Kubernetes Rate Limiting** (Go Implementation)
1. **Token Bucket Rate Limiter** (Client-side)
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol/throttle.go`
   - Wraps golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter
   - Used for API server client requests

2. **API Priority and Fairness (APF) System**
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`
   - Manages FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects
   - Dynamic borrowing of concurrency capacity between priority levels
   - Rebalancing every 10 seconds

3. **Fair Queuing Implementation**
   - `stagin

\"## Rate Limiting Implementation Patterns in Envoy and Kubernetes\\n\\n### Envoy Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\nEnvoy implements rate limiting at three distinct filter levels:\\n\\n**1. HTTP Local Rate Limit Filter**\\nThe HTTP local rate limit filter (source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/) implements per-request rate limiting using a token bucket algorithm. The FilterConfig class in local_ratelimit.h manages configuration of token bucket parameters (max_tokens, fill_interval, tokens_per_fill). The implementation supports both global and per-connection rate limiting modes controlled by the `local_rate_limit_per_downstream_connection` configuration parameter.\\n\\n**2. Token Bucket Implementation**\\nThe actual token bucket mechanism is implemented in source/extensions/filters/common/local_ratelimit/local_ratelimit_impl.h through the LocalRateLimiterImpl and RateLimitTokenBucket classes. This design separates the common rate limiting logic from filter-specific configuration, allowing token buckets to be reused across listener, network, and HTTP filters. The implementation includes support for dynamic descriptors using an LRU cache (DynamicDescriptor and DynamicDescriptorMap classes).\\n\\n**3. Global Rate Limit Service Client (Rate Limit Quota Service)**\\nEnvoy provides a distributed rate limiting solution through the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS) protocol implemented in source/extensions/filters/http/rate_limit_quota/. The GlobalRateLimitClientImpl class (global_client_impl.h/cc) handles bidirectional gRPC streaming with the RLQS server, managing quota buckets across worker threads. The LocalRateLimitClientImpl (client_impl.h/cc) provides per-worker thread access to the global rate limit client via thread-local storage. The quota bucket cache (quota_bucket_cache.h) stores quota information and coordinates between the global and local clients.\\n\\n**4. Network and Listener Level Filters**\\nEnvoy also provides rate limiting at the network (source/extensions/filters/network/local_ratelimit/) and listener (source/extensions/filters/listener/local_ratelimit/) levels, allowing rate limiting to be applied before HTTP processing or even before TLS handshake, using the same token bucket implementation pattern.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\n**1. Token Bucket Rate Limiter (Client-Side)**\\nKubernetes client-go library implements a token bucket rate limiter in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol/throttle.go. The NewTokenBucketRateLimiter function wraps the golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter to provide a rate limiter that allows burst traffic while maintaining a smooth QPS. The tokenBucketRateLimiter struct wraps rate.Limiter and adds clock support for testability.\\n\\n**2. API Priority and Fairness (APF) Controller**\\nThe Kubernetes API server implements sophisticated priority and fairness handling through the APF controller in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go. The configController class watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects from the flowcontrol API group. The controller manages priorityLevelState objects for each priority level, implementing dynamic borrowing of concurrency capacity between priority levels through the updateBorrowing method called periodically every 10 seconds.\\n\\n**3. Fair Queuing Implementation**\\nThe core queueing logic is implemented in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/, implementing the fair queuing for server requests technique. The queueSet class maintains separate queues for each flow schema, tracking virtual finish times and seats (concurrency units) using virtual clock calculations. This ensures fair resource allocation across different priority levels and flow schemas.\\n\\n**4. Priority Level Configuration**\\nPriority levels are defined in staging/src/k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1/types.go and related versioned API types. Each PriorityLevelConfiguration specifies whether requests are exempt from limits (PriorityLevelEnablementExempt) or subject to concurrency limits (PriorityLevelEnablementLimited), with nominalConcurrencyShares controlling the fair share allocation.\\n\\n**5. APF Filter**\\nThe apf_filter.go implements the HTTP filter that integrates APF with the HTTP request handling pipeline. The filter classifies incoming requests based on FlowSchema rules, dispatching them to the appropriate priority level queue, and ensuring proper waiting and execution handling.\\n\\n### Key Differences in Patterns\\n\\n**Envoy's approach:**\\n- Uses token bucket as the primary mechanism at all levels\\n- Supports distributed rate limiting via gRPC streaming to a centralized service\\n- Separates local (per-connection/process) and global (distributed) rate limiting\\n- Token buckets are configurable with fill intervals and tokens per fill\\n\\n**Kubernetes' approach:**\\n- Combines token bucket with sophisticated fair queuing for multi-tenant scenarios\\n- Implements priority-based scheduling with dynamic capacity borrowing\\n- Tracks per-request work estimates and concurrency consumption\\n- Uses virtual clock calculations for fair allocation of limited concurrency\\n\"\n}\n",

\"## Rate Limiting Implementation Patterns in Envoy and Kubernetes\\n\\n### Envoy Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\nEnvoy implements rate limiting at three distinct filter levels:\\n\\n**1. HTTP Local Rate Limit Filter**\\nThe HTTP local rate limit filter (source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/) implements per-request rate limiting using a token bucket algorithm. The FilterConfig class in local_ratelimit.h manages configuration of token bucket parameters (max_tokens, fill_interval, tokens_per_fill). The implementation supports both global and per-connection rate limiting modes controlled by the `local_rate_limit_per_downstream_connection` configuration parameter.\\n\\n**2. Token Bucket Implementation**\\nThe actual token bucket mechanism is implemented in source/extensions/filters/common/local_ratelimit/local_ratelimit_impl.h through the LocalRateLimiterImpl and RateLimitTokenBucket classes. This design separates the common rate limiting logic from filter-specific configuration, allowing token buckets to be reused across listener, network, and HTTP filters. The implementation includes support for dynamic descriptors using an LRU cache (DynamicDescriptor and DynamicDescriptorMap classes).\\n\\n**3. Global Rate Limit Service Client (Rate Limit Quota Service)**\\nEnvoy provides a distributed rate limiting solution through the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS) protocol implemented in source/extensions/filters/http/rate_limit_quota/. The GlobalRateLimitClientImpl class (global_client_impl.h/cc) handles bidirectional gRPC streaming with the RLQS server, managing quota buckets across worker threads. The LocalRateLimitClientImpl (client_impl.h/cc) provides per-worker thread access to the global rate limit client via thread-local storage. The quota bucket cache (quota_bucket_cache.h) stores quota information and coordinates between the global and local clients.\\n\\n**4. Network and Listener Level Filters**\\nEnvoy also provides rate limiting at the network (source/extensions/filters/network/local_ratelimit/) and listener (source/extensions/filters/listener/local_ratelimit/) levels, allowing rate limiting to be applied before HTTP processing or even before TLS handshake, using the same token bucket implementation pattern.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\n**1. Token Bucket Rate Limiter (Client-Side)**\\nKubernetes client-go library implements a token bucket rate limiter in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol/throttle.go. The NewTokenBucketRateLimiter function wraps the golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter to provide a rate limiter that allows burst traffic while maintaining a smooth QPS. The tokenBucketRateLimiter struct wraps rate.Limiter and adds clock support for testability.\\n\\n**2. API Priority and Fairness (APF) Controller**\\nThe Kubernetes API server implements sophisticated priority and fairness handling through the APF controller in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go. The configController class watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects from the flowcontrol API group. The controller manages priorityLevelState objects for each priority level, implementing dynamic borrowing of concurrency capacity between priority levels through the updateBorrowing method called periodically every 10 seconds.\\n\\n**3. Fair Queuing Implementation**\\nThe core queueing logic is implemented in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/, implementing the fair queuing for server requests technique. The queueSet class maintains separate queues for each flow schema, tracking virtual finish times and seats (concurrency units) using virtual clock calculations. This ensures fair resource allocation across different priority levels and flow schemas.\\n\\n**4. Priority Level Configuration**\\nPriority levels are defined in staging/src/k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1/types.go and related versioned API types. Each PriorityLevelConfiguration specifies whether requests are exempt from limits (PriorityLevelEnablementExempt) or subject to concurrency limits (PriorityLevelEnablementLimited), with nominalConcurrencyShares controlling the fair share allocation.\\n\\n**5. APF Filter**\\nThe apf_filter.go implements the HTTP filter that integrates APF with the HTTP request handling pipeline. The filter classifies incoming requests based on FlowSchema rules, dispatching them to the appropriate priority level queue, and ensuring proper waiting and execution handling.\\n\\n### Key Differences in Patterns\\n\\n**Envoy's approach:**\\n- Uses token bucket as the primary mechanism at all levels\\n- Supports distributed rate limiting via gRPC streaming to a centralized service\\n- Separates local (per-connection/process) and global (distributed) rate limiting\\n- Token buckets are configurable with fill intervals and tokens per fill\\n\\n**Kubernetes' approach:**\\n- Combines token bucket with sophisticated fair queuing for multi-tenant scenarios\\n- Implements priority-based scheduling with dynamic capacity borrowing\\n- Tracks per-request work estimates and concurrency consumption\\n- Uses virtual clock calculations for fair allocation of limited concurrency\\n\"\n}\n",
